Well Evaluation
Marathon Oil Company
Hazel 14-8H
Figure 1. Ensign #161 drilling the Hazel 14-8H, November 2014
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company Hazel 14-8H [NW NW Section 17, T144N, R96W] is located
approximately 7 miles northwest of Manning in Dunn County, North Dakota (Figure 1). The
Hazel 14-8H is a single lateral, double section horizontal well that's part of a multi-well pad, and
has a target pay zone in the Mississippian-Devonian Middle Bakken Member. The Middle
Bakken is known as a mixed carbonate-clastic sequence stratigraphically sequenced between two
petroliferous, carbonaceous black shales, the Upper Bakken Shale and the Lower Bakken Shale.
The two shales combined serve as the prospects source rock.
PLAN
The drilling plan stipulated that the vertical hole inclination should be held at an inclination of
1.50º with an azimuth of 40° from surface casing, at 2,328', until approximately 10,380' MD
where the curve would be kicked-off for a 12º per 100' curve until landing, at approximately
11,179' MD (10,886' TVD). Prognosis estimated the landing target to be 15' below the base of
the Upper Bakken Shale. After landing, intermediate casing would then be set and cemented to
isolate the target reservoir, and the lateral would commence. The lateral would continue north at
approximately 359º to a bottom hole location within NW NW of Section 5, T144N-R96W.
OFFSET WELLS
Top and thickness control was provided by 4 main offsets (Figure 2). The following offset wells
provided gamma signatures to correlate formation tops; allowing thickness evaluation for a
proper target landing, and provided gamma signature and structure control during lateral
operations. The previously, batch drilled Knopik 24-8H also provided lateral control.
The Marathon Oil Company Louie Hendricks 24-20H. The wellhead is located approximately
2 miles south of the subject well, and it was a horizontal Middle Bakken well drilled in June
of 2009. The horizontal path of the wellbore parallels the path of the Hazel 14-8H, so this
offset will be used to compare structure and gamma.
The Davis Oil Co. Murphy Creek State 1 is located approximately 1.3 miles east of the Hazel
14-8H, and was completed in December of 1983. The Murphy Creek State 1 was a vertical
hole drilled down to the Duperow formation, and was classified as a dry hole. This offset is
used to land the well and see the entire Middle Bakken gamma signature.
The Marathon Oil Company Kerkhoff 14-8H is located on the same pad as the subject well,
and had the vertical-curve section completed prior to the subject well.
Figure 2. Map showing the location of the Marathon Oil Company Hazel 14-8H and the location of the four
wells used for offset control.
ENGINEERING
The Hazel 14-8H well was spud by rig Ensign #161 on September 9, 2014, drilling a 13.5" hole
with freshwater to a depth of 2,343' MD. Here, 9 5/8" surface casing was set and cemented to
2,328' MD. The vertical hole continued on October 15, drilling with diesel invert fluid weighing
9.7 to 11.2 pounds/gallon and two assemblies to a kick-off point of 10,346' MD. At this depth,
the curve was kicked off using a 2.12° mud motor. The curve concluded after 11.6 hours, using
a single assembly, drilling to 11,273' MD (10,885' TVD). After completing the curve section of
the well, 7" casing was set and cemented to 11,223' MD. On November 10, in preparation for
the lateral portion of the well, invert diesel drilling fluid was displaced with salt water drilling
fluid. Two separate assemblies, using 6" PDC bits and BHI X-treme motors, were used to drill
the lateral section from 11,273'MD to a total depth of 21,430' MD in 89.2 hours.
The Hazel 14-8H reached total depth of 21,430' on November 16, 2014, at a closure direction of
358.99° and a true vertical depth (TVD) of 10,948'. The bottom hole location was estimated to
be 10,925.32' north and 192.83' west of the surface location or approximately 219.20' FNL and
908.17' FWL, Lot 4 Section 5, T144N, R96W (Figure 3.)

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods
A two-person geology team logged drill cuttings, monitored mud gas and provided guidance for
steering. Sample and gas evaluation began in the Kibbey Formation at 8,670' MD. Rig crew
members caught 30' lagged samples under direction of the well-site geologists. Wet and dry
cuttings were examined under a binocular microscope. Two sets of dry cuttings were collected
and sent to Marathon Oil Company and the North Dakota Geological Survey. A digital gas
detector (total gas with chromatograph) was interfaced with a Pason electronic data recorder
(EDR). The Pason EDR provided hole depth, bit depth and pump stroke information to the gas
detection program (MController) and distributed the detector's total gas information for viewing
across location. Total mud gas was recorded in units (100 units = 1% methane equivalent in air)
and chromatography of C1 ­ C4 components were calculated in parts-per-million.
Lithology
Beginning in the Mississippian Kibbey Formation of the Big Snowy Group, sample collection
and logging continued into the Mississippian-Devonian Middle Bakken. The False Bakken
interval and the Bakken Formation are the only strata discussed in detail here, complete sample
descriptions by depth can be found in an addendum to this report.
The Bakken Formation, Upper Bakken Shale Member was penetrated at 10,859' TVD (-8,738'
MSL). This member is easily recognized by a sharp increase and sustained high gamma ray
counts, a marked increase in penetration rates, and typically sustained higher gas shows. The
Upper Bakken Shale is a black, petroliferous shale containing occasional to common
disseminated and nodular pyrite (Figure 4). The Middle Bakken Member was penetrated at
10,872' TVD (-8,451' MSL). The Middle Bakken consists of a light to medium gray-brown,
silty sandstone, containing fine intergranular porosity and light spotty brown oil staining (Figure
5). The top of this member was picked from a combination of decreased gamma counts,
decreased total gas, and a decrease in penetration rates.
Figures 4 & 5: Wet cuttings of Upper Bakken shale (left) and Middle Bakken silty sandstone (right).
Geosteering
The well prognosis called for a landing target 15' into the Middle Bakken Member, at a depth of
10,872' TVD. Using gamma signatures from offset wells, well-site geologists were able to
correlate formation tops in order to make any necessary corrections to the prognosis landing
target. Lodgepole markers came in consistently low to prognosis, and the decision was made to
lower the landing target a total of 15' to 10,887' TVD. The actual curve landing came in at
10,885' TVD, landing the well-bore 2' into the 8' geologic window.
Three primary gamma signatures were used to steer the well in the 8' thick geologic window.
Throughout our target interval, gamma counts ranged from roughly 60-100 (API), and oscillated
with regularity. This gamma trend was pervasive throughout our entire zone which proposed a
challenge determining our precise location within the target, in the laminated facies. Two other
primary markers used to steer the wellbore were observed above and below our target zone.
Above the zone, a reliable packestone layer, gamma marker was observed. Gamma counts in
this packestone layer registered considerably lower, to around 30 (API). This layer became less
pronounced later in the lateral, but packstone stringers were still present. Ooids were also
observed in this packestone layer, which differentiated it from our target zone. At the bottom of
our target interval, an increased, tighter gamma signature was observed with counts of 75-85
(API). This marker bounded our target zone below and was encountered several times
throughout the lateral portion of the well. These markers provided data upon which formation
dip was calculated, and were consistent throughout the lateral.
The target window was entered at approximately 11,200' MD, and the well-bore was maintained
in the target for approximately 75% of the lateral. Over the course of the lateral the center line of
our target dropped a total of 53' TVD over 10,315', resulting in a gross apparent dip of -0.29°
(Figure 6)

Hydrocarbons
Gas shows increased significantly towards the bottom of the Lodgepole Formation. Several gas
shows over 3,000 units were observed while drilling the curve through the lower Lodgepole,
False Bakken, and Upper Bakken Shale Member. These shows can most likely be attributed to
high hydrocarbon content in the Upper Bakken Shale, as well as zones of possible fracture
porosity towards the bottom of the Lodgepole Formation.
Background gas throughout the lateral ranged from 500-3,000 units, with an average of around
1,800 units. Several intervals of the lateral produced notable increases in background gas and gas
shows, though there is little evidence to link high gas shows to a particular portion of our drilling
window (Figure 7). These increases are likely a result of localized zones of high pressure and
porosity, and possible fracture porosity. Green-brown oil was observed coming over the shakers
throughout the lateral, especially after the trip at 18,238' MD.
Gas was circulated through the gas buster for the duration of the lateral. A 2-4' intermittent flare
was observed during the first portion of the lateral and gradually transitioned to a 3-7' constant
flare by total depth. No back-pressure was held during the Hazel 14-8H lateral.

SUMMARY
The Hazel 14-8H is a successfully drilled Middle Bakken, horizontal well in Murphy Creek
Field. The well was completed in 17 days, reaching a total depth of 21,430' on November 16,
2014. Samples from the Middle Bakken consisted of light to medium gray-brown silty sandstone
with fine intergranular porosity and light, spotty brown oil staining. Background gas values
ranged between 500 and 3,000 units, with an average of 1800 units, throughout the lateral. Mud
was circulated through the gas buster for the duration of the lateral, resulting in a 2-7' flare and a
20' trip flare observed at 18,238' MD. No back-pressure was held while drilling the well. The
overall apparent down-dip was 0.29°, with the well-bore remaining in target for 75% of the
lateral, exposing 7,669' to the pay zone. The well is currently awaiting completion operations to
maximize production.
Respectfully submitted,
Nathan Stansfield
Anna Bruckmeier
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
November 19, 2014

LITHOLOGY
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A
detailed list of sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma ray
marker tops have been inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined
wet and dry under a binocular microscope. The drilling fluid was diesel based invert from surface casing
to 11,273' and changed to salt-water from 11,273' to 21,430' TD. Sample collection began at 8,670'.
Kibbey Formation
8670-8700 SILTSTONE: red-brown, red-orange, firm to friable, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, poorly cemented,
sandy in part
8700-8730 SILTSTONE: red-brown, red-orange, firm to friable, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, poorly cemented,
sandy in part
Kibbey "Lime"
8,751' MD; 8,748' TVD (-6,327')
8730-8760 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, cream, friable to firm, earthy texture, no visible
porosity; rare ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, microcrystalline in part, soft, amorphous texture
8760-8790 SILTSTONE: red-brown, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, poorly cemented, sandy in part;
occasional LIMESTONE: as above
8790-8820 SILTSTONE: red-brown, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, poorly cemented, sandy in part
8820-8850 SILTSTONE: red-brown, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, poorly cemented, sandy in part
8850-8880 SILTSTONE: red-brown, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, poorly cemented, sandy in part; rare
ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, microcrystalline in part, soft, amorphous texture
Charles Formation: 1st Salt
8,909' MD; 8.906' TVD (-6,485')
8880-8910 SALT: clear to translucent, crystalline, hard; SILTSTONE: red-orange to red-brown, firm, sub-blocky,
calcite cemented, poorly cemented, sandy in part; occasional rare ANHYDRITE: off white to cream,
microcrystalline in part, soft, amorphous texture
8910-8940 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray, cream, microcrystalline, firm, earthy texture, argillaceous in part,
no visible porosity; common ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, microcrystalline in part, soft, amorphous texture
8940-8970 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray, cream, microcrystalline, firm, earthy texture, argillaceous in part,
no visible porosity; ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, microcrystalline in part, soft, amorphous texture
8970-9000 SALT: clear to translucent, crystalline, hard

Dear Natalie:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 22900, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200'
setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 1280 acre
spacing unit consisting of Sections 8 & 5 T144N R96W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Marathon may set conductor on permitted wells only. Effective June 1, 2014, a
covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site
beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back
whenever filtration operations are conducted. In cases where a spacing unit is accessed from an off-site drill
pad, an affidavit must be provided affirming that the surface owner of the multi-well pad agrees to accept
burial on their property of the cuttings generated from drilling the wells into an offsite spacing unit.
MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Nicole Nelson at 701-290-1527 prior to location
construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling
and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent
pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are
prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill
cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing point is:
551 N. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10994
N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be
waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to
evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that
would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the
applicant should retain the permit.
Natalie Menge
June 23, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck,
via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling
contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m.
to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must
be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the
directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the
director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a
certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or
when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby
granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date
the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records
wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the
Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them,
complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to have access at all times to
any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect producing and drilling wells. Any
information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The information so
obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission
and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours,
and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the
plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well
bore, and (3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic
cement evaluation log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior
to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format)
copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or
attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

Dear Todd,
Please find attached the documents that accompany the APD for the above captioned wel . This
application was submitted using the e-filing process on-line. Please process the APD and use the
Credit Card Marathon has on file with your office for the processing fee.
As per the address request issue, we have contacted Denise Brew, Dunn County Emergency
Manager , to request a legal street address for these wells per the requirements in NDAC 43-02-
03-16.
Please keep all information confidential
If you have any questions or require more information, please contact Natalie Menge, Bill Groffy
or Joe Schneider Regulatory Compliance Representatives at 701-456-7500
nmenge@marathonoil.com, wfgroffy@marathonoil.com or JJSchneider@Marathonoil.com.
Thank You.
